Jamison Brereton

44 (485)
Indra
┼Ъaс╣Гyu B─Бrhaspatya
24 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ6, triс╣гс╣нubh or vir─Бj 7, 9, vir─Бj 8, triс╣гс╣нubh 10тАУ24, arranged in trcas ╠е
A composite hymn placed toward the end of the Indra cycle in Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI, the hymn consists of eight tr╠еcas, the first two (vss. 1тАУ6) in anuс╣гс╣нubh, the third (vss. 7тАУ9) in a mixture of triс╣гс╣нubh and vir─Бj, and the remaining five (vss. 10тАУ24) in triс╣гс╣нubh. Several of the tr╠еcas are rhetorically unified: 1тАУ3 with its repeated second half-verse following a definitional relative clause; 19тАУ21 with its insistent тАЬbullтАЭ theme; 22тАУ24 with its repeated half-verse-initial тАЬthis one hereтАЭ (ay├бm) referring to soma. The others have less obvious internal unity, though there is often a continuity of theme or subject. There is also no visible external unity among the tr╠еcas collected in this тАЬhymn,тАЭ though it seldom strays far from Indra and the soma-drinking, the topic of many of the immediately preceding hymns. Indeed, Oldenberg (1888: 203) suggests that VI.44 owes its position to the similarity between the refrain of its first tr╠еca and the refrain of VI.43.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOpulent Indra, the Soma that abounds with riches, and is most resplendent with glories, is poured out; it is your exhilaration, Indra, lord of the offering.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Lord of the offering: svadh─Бpati = cherisher or protector of the Soma libation, svadh─Бy─Б annasya somalakс╣гaс╣Зasya p─Бlan─Бt

Jamison Brereton

The one that is wealthiest, o wealthy one, that is most brilliant through its brilliance,
the pressed somaтАФthat is your exhilarating drink, o Indra, lord of
independent power.

Griffith

THAT which is wealthiest, Wealthy God in splendoursmost illustrious,
Soma is pressed: thy gladdening draught, Indra! libation’s Lord! is this.

Geldner

Der ausgepre├Яte Soma, der der reichste, o Reicher, der an Glanz der glanzvollste ist, er ist dein Rauschtrank, Indra, Herr des Lebenssaftes.

Grassmann

Der reichste Soma, reichster du, der herrlichste an Herrlichkeit, Der ist, o Indra, dir gebraut, der Rauschtrank, o du Opferherr.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe divine heaven and earth adore that vigour of his, which our hymns augment, the appropriator of the riches of the foe.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He whom songs make strong, the lord of overpowering generosityтАФ his tempestuous force do the two world-halves, the goddesses, respect. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ├нd in p─Бda a seems displaced: we would expect y├бm ├нd тАж, though that order would produce a choppy meter. The ├нd in c is better positioned, though we actually might expect it to be limiting asya, not the t├бm anticipating ┼Ы├║с╣гmam. The published translation does not render either ├нd; if I were to do so, the result would be тАЬ(ItтАЩs) just (him) whom the songs make strong тАж just his tempestuous force that the worldhalves respect.тАЭ

Although this tс╣Ыca does not have glaring signs of unity, it particularly concerns the songs that strengthen Indra and rouse his aid to us. It also has a subtle morphological ring; see the disc. of the loc. inf. in 3d.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Worshippers), the efficacy of your eulogy is to be manifested to that Indra, whose protections, like (those) of a sensible man, are displayed as abiding along with him.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vipo na, medh─Бvirat iva, that is, the protective measures or expedients of a sensible or wise man are capable for all affairs, sarva k─Бryaku┼Ыalaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

It (is mine) to lay on your behalf, with the power of solemn speech, the underlayer for Indra,
whose forms of helps are like inspired words, since, dwelling together, they spread apart in their ascent. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is syntactically more complex and ritually more technical than the other two vss. in this tс╣Ыca.

The most noteworthy form is the loc. inf. upastс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бni, a hapax, not surprisingly. In my opinion it is possible to account for the creation of this form from context, albeit indirectly. The first vs. of this tс╣Ыca contains the well-attested 1st sg.

gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├й (4b), belonging to the tight class of -s├й 1st sgs. in the тАШpraise/singтАЩ semantic sphere. Beside gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├й there exists a -с╣г├бni infinitive gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi (2x, incl. once in this maс╣Зс╕Нala, VI.15.6). I think our poet built upastс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi on the model of this gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бс╣Зi, as a partial echo of gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├й in 4b, based on the existence of 9th class presents to both of these roots. Because it echoes that 1st sg. I interpr. the predicated inf. with 1st ps. ref.

(тАЬit [is mine] to lay тАжтАЭ). Once again, as in 4, the vaс╕е refers to the poetтАЩs fellow officiants.

In the ritual the тАШunderlayerтАЩ is the layer of butter spread on the ladle underneath the principal offering. Here it is used in a doubly metaphorical sense: the underlayer for Indra could presumably be configured physically as the barhis on which he would sit, but at another metaphorical remove it could refer to the recitations that provide him with a figurative foundation.

The poet then, by a clever trick, mobilizes this underlayer of words to serve as a metaphor for the multiplication of IndraтАЩs forms of help for us. This is accomplished by means of a simile: v├нpo n├б тАж ┼лt├бyaс╕е тАЬforms of help like inspired words,тАЭ thus implicitly equating the two. These v├нpaс╕е тАШinspired wordsтАЩ (not, with Geldner, тАШfingersтАЩ) are ours, in fact the very ukth├б- found in p─Бda a, dependent on barh├бс╣З─Б.

The connection between the two is suggested by the phrase barh├бс╣З─Б vip├бс╕е тАЬby the power of inspired speechтАЭ in VIII.63.7 (vip├бс╕е there is gen. sg., as opposed to our nom. pl. v├нpaс╕е, as the accent shows). In cd the poet asserts that like our hymns, which rise to Indra, spreading from their position as interconnected (sakс╣г├нtaс╕е тАШdwelling togetherтАЩ) underlayer, his forms of help will similarly grow up and out. On this vs. see also Scarlatta (97).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although this tс╣Ыca does not have glaring signs of unity, it particularly concerns the songs that strengthen Indra and rouse his aid to us. It also has a subtle morphological ring; see the disc. of the loc. inf. in 3d.

Griffith

To seat your Indra, I will spread abroad with power this song of praise.
The saving succours that abide in him, like songs, extend and grow.

тАЬIndra, appreciates him who is skilled (in holy rites); a recent friend, quaffing (the libation), he heaps excellent (wealth) upon the devout; partaking of (the sacrificial) food, (and brought) by his robust agitators (of the earth, his steeds), he, through his benevolence, is a protector to his friends.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The medial pf. part. pap─Бn├б- is one of only 3 forms of the middle pf. in the RV, 2 of which, incl. this one, are used passively. See K├╝mmel (309). Note that a deriv. of the other root тИЪp─Б тАШprotectтАЩ, p─Бy├║с╕е, is found in the 2nd hemistich.

The vs. is notable for a number of hapaxes: acait, staul─Б╠Б-, and dhaut├бr─л, the latter two also marked by vс╣Ыddhi.

On acait as a nonce s-aor. to тИЪcit тАШperceiveтАЩ, see Narten (114).

staul─Б╠Б- here is reminiscent of the likewise impenetrable staun├б- in this same maс╣Зс╕Нala VI.66.5. No remotely credible guesses have been proposed for these forms, or for dhaut├бr─л-; Geldner (n. 7c): тАЬganz dunkelтАЭ and he fails to tr. the NP; Oldenberg: тАЬ├Ьber staul─Б╠Бbhir dhaut├бr─лbhiс╕е scheint kein Ergebnis erreichbarтАЭ; EWA (II.762 and I.783) also throws up its hands. I am inclined to connect staul─Б╠Б- and staun├б- with similar words but with aspirated initial sth-, namely sth┼лr├б- тАШbrawny, sturdyтАЩ and sth┼л╠Бс╣З─Б- тАШpostтАЩ (see comm. ad VI.66.5) respectively, but I cannot explain the phonological discrepancy.

As for dhaut├бr─л-, Oldenberg tentatively suggests that it might belong with one of the roots тИЪdh─Бv тАШrunтАЩ or тАШrinseтАЩ. For translational convenience I have assumed the former, but without any conviction. In any case the striking double vс╣Ыddhi -au- of these paired nominals must be meant to draw attention to the phrase.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Soma, creator (of all), on the path of sacrifice, has been drunk; the worshippers have presented it to gratify the mind (of Indra); may he, the humiliator (of his foes), possessing a vast body, propitiated by our praises, become manifest to our view.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

On the path of truth, the ritual adept has been drunk. The gods have set their minds for glory.
Acquiring the name of тАЬgreatтАЭ by (ritual) speeches, the one worthy of the quest has disclosed his wondrous form to be seen. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The passive interpr. of the pf. part. pap─Бn├б- in 7b is affirmed by the pass.

aor. ap─Бyi in 8a.

Similarly, the second p─Бda clarifies the sense of 7b, where it was said that soma тАЬhas perceived what is better for the gods.тАЭ What is better seems to be the godsтАЩ intent, announced here in 8b, to achieve glory. The VP m├бnas тИЪkс╣Ы generally means тАШset oneтАЩs mind on/toтАЩ; cf. V.61.7, I.54.9, II.26.2=VIII.19.20 (though V.30.4 and X.117.2 are outliers).

The forms grouped by Grassmann under a stem mah├бs-, an adj. meaning тАШgrossтАЩ, generally have other interpr., either adverbial or belonging to a diff. stem (e.g., gen. sg. to m├бh-). Although a suffix-accented adj. mah├бs- built by accent shift to neut.

m├бhas- тАШgreatnessтАЩ would fit the standard pattern (type y├б┼Ыas- тАШgloryтАЩ ├а ya┼Ы├бs- тАШgloriousтАЩ), the realization of the pattern in this lexical item seems to have been rare to non-existent. In this passage most (Grassmann, Geldner) do take mah├бс╕е as a neut. adj. to this stem, modifying n─Б╠Бma (тАЬacquiring a great nameтАЭ), but because of the general avoidance of such an adj. I prefer to take mah├бс╕е as the masc. nom. sg. to mah├б-, a quotation of the name he received.

In keeping with the interpr. of the root тИЪven as тАШtrack, trace, seekтАЩ, I interpr.

its grdv. veny├б-, when not a PN, as тАШ(worthy) to be tracked/soughtтАЩ.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the meter of this tс╣Ыca see Oldenberg, Proleg. 91 and Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition metrical comm. The fading in and out between Vir─Бj and Triс╣гс╣нubh is further complicated by the openings of 3 in 11-syllable lines in 7b, c.

The tс╣Ыca concerns soma and contains lexical and thematic responsions.

Griffith

In course of Law the sapient juice was quaffed: the Deities to glory turned their mind.
Winning through hymns a lofty title, he, the Lovely, made his beauteous form apparent.

English translation:

тАЬBestow upon us most brilliant vigour; oppose the numerous enemies of your worshippers; gran us, for our pious acts, abundant food; secure us in the enjoyment of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bestow the most brilliant skill on us. Repel the many hostilities of the peoples.
Make our vitality higher through your abilities. Help us in the winning of the stake. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca-final vs. reprises and repurposes some of the statements in the opening vs. 7. The skill (d├бkс╣гa-) that Soma found in 7a we ask him to bestow on us in 9a. Soma, тАЬhaving wonтАЭ (sasav─Б╠Бn) in 7c, is asked to help us in winning (s─Бta├║ тАж aviс╕Нс╕Нhi) in 9d. Unfortunately nothing in 9 sheds light on the problematic instr. phrase in 7c.

VI.44.10-12: This tс╣Ыca foresees various disasters and tribulations and asks Indra for his help in combatting them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the meter of this tс╣Ыca see Oldenberg, Proleg. 91 and Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition metrical comm. The fading in and out between Vir─Бj and Triс╣гс╣нubh is further complicated by the openings of 3 in 11-syllable lines in 7b, c.

The tс╣Ыca concerns soma and contains lexical and thematic responsions.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, possessor of affluence, we have recourse to you, the bountiful, lord of steeds, be not unfavourable to us; no other kinsman is beheld (by us) among men; who else have they called yo the bestower of wealth?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, we have become ready just for you, the giver, you generous possessor of the fallow bays. Do not lose the track.
No one has shown himself as our friend among mortals. Do they not call you a rouser (even) of the weak? с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am not sure of the exact nuance of тИЪbh┼л + DAT. Grassmann takes it as meaning тАШangeh├╢ren, eigen seinтАЩ, with a rare dat. here, instead of the gen. usual in this idiom (his no. 13). Geldner renders it thus (тАЬdir тАж haben wir uns zu eigen gegebenтАЭ). Even with the gen., Grassmann identifies very few passage with this value, and most of these should be otherwise interpr., and I also wonder about an augmented aor. in such a sense. The published translation is by contrast тАЬwe have become ready for you,тАЭ and I think something like this is the intention (perhaps тАЬwe are here for youтАЭ). We are awaiting his advent at the ritual and the generosity he will display there, but there is some worry that he will fail to show up, as the 2nd clause of the 1st hemistich shows.

Note that the fairly rare root тИЪven appears here soon after the appearance of its deriv. veny├б- in 8d. It is possible that this lexical association led to the grafting of this tс╣Ыca onto the previous one in this loose collection of short hymns.

Griffith

We turn to thee as Giver, liberal Indra. Lord of the Bay Steeds, be not thou ungracious.
No friend among mankind have we to lookto: why have men called thee him who spurs the niggard?

Geldner

Indra, dir dem Schenker haben wir uns zu eigen gegeben, du gabenreicher Falbenlenker. Wende deinen Blick nicht ab! Unter den Sterblichen hat sich kein Freund gezeigt. Warum nennt man gerade dich den Ermutiger des Schwachen?

Grassmann

Wir sind zu eigen, Indra, dir, dem Geber; nicht kehr dich ab, o m├дcht’ger Rosselenker; Nicht unter Menschen zeigt der rechte Freund sich; warum sonst nennt man dich der Matten Kr├дft’ger?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGive us not up, showerer (of benefits), to the obstructor (of our rites); relying upon the friendship of you, lord of riches, may we be unharmed; many are the hindrances (opposed) to you among men; slay those who make no libations, root out those who present no offerings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Give us not to exhaustion, bull. Let us not come to harm in our comradeship with you, the wealthy.
Many are the tributes for you among the peoples, Indra. Smite the
non-pressers; rip away those who donтАЩt deliver. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

On niс╣гс╣г├нdh- see comm. ad III.51.5.

Griffith

Give us not up, Strong Hero! to the hungry: unharmed be we whom thou, so rich, befriendest.
Full many a boon hast thou for men demolish those who present no gifts nor pour oblations.

Geldner

Liefere uns nicht einem Hungerleider aus, o Bulle, nicht sollten wir in deiner, des Reichen, Freundschaft Schaden erleiden. Du, Indra, hast eine reiche Dankesschuld bei den Menschen. Erschlage die, die nicht Soma opfern; rotte die Knauser aus!

Grassmann

Gesell uns nicht dem D├╝rft’gen zu, o starker, nicht geh’s uns schlecht in deiner Huld, des reichen; Viel Gaben hast du, Indra, f├╝r die Menschen; Gottlose t├╢dte, tilg’ die Opferlosen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрднреНрд░рд╛рдгреАрд╡ рд╕реНрддрдирдпрдиреН рдЧрд░реНрдЬрдпрдиреН рдкрд░реНрдЬрдиреНрдпреЛ рдпрдерд╛ рдореЗрдШрд╛рдиреБрджреНрдЧрдордпрддреНрдпреЗрд╡рдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЧреЛрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдореВрд╣рджреНрд╡рдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЙрддреН рдЗрдпрд░реНрддрд┐ рдЙрджреАрд░рдпрддрд┐ ред рдЙрджреНрдЧрдордпрддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпреЛ рджрд╛рддреБрдореН ред рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╛рд░реНрдзрдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддрдГ ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдХрд╛рд░реБрдзрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдХрд╛рд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрд╕рд┐ рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдордШреЛрдирдГ рдзрдирд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рдХреГрдкрдгрд╛рдГ рдЕрджрд╛рдорд╛рдирдГ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдорджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ рдорд╛ рдЖ рджрднрдиреН рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рд╖реБрдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╡рдЪрдирд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпрдГред рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рдзрдирд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs Indra, when thundering rases the clouds, so he (heaps upon his worshippers) riches of horses and cattle; yo, Indra, are he ancient upholder of the sacrificer; let not the opulent wrong you, not presenting (oblations).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like the thunderer the rain clouds, Indra stirs up bounties of horses and cattle.
It is you who provide nourishment to the bard from of old. Let those without gifts not trick you away from (our) benefactor. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The morphological identity and syntactic function of magh├│naс╕е in d are unclear. See esp. OldenbergтАЩs disc. It can be either acc. pl. or gen.-abl. sg. (or an irregular nom. pl., a possibility that Oldenberg considers and dismisses). The problem is that in neither case would it form part of a standard construction with the verb ─Б╠БтИЪdabh. Geldner (n. 12d) thinks of a double acc.: тАЬtrick (our) benefactors out of youтАЭ – that is, the non-giving ones might scare Indra off from our sacrifice or get their invitation to him first, thereby depriving our maghavans of IndraтАЩs presence. This certainly conforms to a regular worry that sacrificers express, but the construction is unprecedented. Oldenberg opts for the abl. sg. The purport of his interpr. is essentially the same as GeldnerтАЩs: that the non-givers not trick Indra away from (abl.) the maghavan, which he sees as our human patron. The published translation follows Oldenberg, though it might be clearer if it were тАЬтАж not trick you away from (our) benefactor.тАЭ Although this construction is also unprecedented, adding an oblique complement to a transitive construction seems less radical to me than investing it with a second acc. However, I now see another problem with the Oldenberg solution: the tс╣Ыca opens with a voc. maghavan addressed to Indra (10a), so it might be odd to have another sg. form of this stem referring to a human. And I donтАЩt see how to construe an abl. magh├│naс╕е referring to Indra in the same construction that contains an acc. tv─Б with the same reference. Nevertheless, I still favor OldenbergтАЩs interpr. and simply allow for this shift of reference; such a shift from divine to human is also necessary if the form is taken as plural, with Geldner There is another possibility, raised and dismissed by Oldenberg, that magh├│naс╕е is in fact acc. pl., but the two acc. are conjoined: тАЬm├╢gen nicht die Nichtgeber dich betr├╝gen (und) die Spender.тАЭ This is not outside the realm of possibility.

Griffith

As Indra thundering impels the rain-clouds, so doth he send us store of kine and horses.
Thou art of old the Cherisher of singers let not the rich who bring no gifts deceive thee.

Geldner

Wie der Donnerer die Wolken, so l├д├Яt Indra die Schenkungen von Rossen und Rindern steigen. L├дngst bist du der Brotgeber des Dichters. Nicht sollen die Kargen die Freigebigen um dich betr├╝gen.

Grassmann

Wie Regenwolken sendet Indra donnernd Geschenke uns an Rossen und an Rindern, Du bist von Alters her der Dichter Schirmherr, nicht k├╝mmern dich die gabenlosen Reichen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMinistrant priests offer libations to the mighty Indra, for he is their king, he who has been exalted by the ancient and recent hymns of adoring sages.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Adhvaryu, hero, give of the pressed (soma drinks) to great Indra, for he is its king,
he who has grown strong by the previous and the present songs of singing seers. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich contains disharmony of number in a constructio ad sensum: The priest is urged to offer of the pressed (soma-drink)s in the plural (sut─Б╠Бn─Бm); the reason for this is immediately given in the 2nd part of p─Бda b, s├б hy ├аsya r─Б╠Бj─Б тАЬfor he is its king.тАЭ Unaccented singular asya presupposes a referent already in the discourse, with тАЬitтАЭ referring to soma, represented in the previous clause as a plural. The singular is then continued in the rest of the tс╣Ыca (asy├б 14a, t├бm тАж s├│mam 14cd, sut├бm тАж s├│mam 15a, with sg. sut├бm picking up pl. sut─Б╠Бn─Бm of 13a).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn the exhilaration of this Soma, the wise Indra, irresistible, has destroyed numerous opposing enemies; offer the sweet-flavoured beverage to that hero, the handsome-chinned, to drink.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In its exhilaration, knowing many shapes, Indra smashed unopposable obstacles.
Pour forth for him the honeyed soma, for the belipped hero to drink. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner point out (n. 14a), the тАЬmany shapesтАЭ (pur├║ v├бrp─Бс╣Гsi) that Indra knows could either be his own (given his penchant for shape-shifting) or those of the various demonic enemies he destroys. I assume that the poet meant to leave it ambiguous, though itтАЩs worth noting that the one instance of the bahuvr─лhi puruv├бrpas- refers to Indra (though in the late hymn X.120.6).

The hapax -si impv. hoс╣гi has no structural support in the RV, the only aor.

attested being the pass. aor. ├бh─Бvi. However, an act. s-aor. is reasonably well attested in Vedic prose, beginning with the BYV Saс╣Гhit─Бs (ahauс╣г─лt, etc.); see Narten (Sig.Aor. 288). It is difficult to know whether yoс╣гi is indirect evidence for a s-aor.

subjunctive to this aor., *hoс╣гat, etc., to which hoс╣гi would ultimately belong, or whether it was created as a nonce beside the other -si impvs. in this ritual sphere such as y├бkс╣гi, m├бtsi and has nothing to do with the aor. forms in prose. I weakly favor the latter explanation.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra be the drinker of this effused Soma, and, exhilarated by it, become the destroyer of Vс╣Ыtra by the thunderbolt; may he come, although from afar, to our sacrifice, (he who is) the giver of dwellings, the upholder of the celebrator (of religious).тАЭ

Let Indra be the one who drinks the pressed soma, who smashes the obstacle [/Vr╠еtra] with his mace in his exhilaration,
who goes to the sacrifice, even from far away, who is the good helper of insights, providing nourishment to the bard. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. is characterized by three root-accented agent nouns (p─Б╠Бt─Б a, h├бnt─Б b, g├бnt─Б c), all p─Бda-initial, all with acc. obj./goal. Then in d the pattern is switched: a suffix-accented agent noun (avit─Б╠Б), interior in its p─Бda (immed. after caesura) with (objective) gen. complement. All of them are presumably predicates of astu in p─Бda a. I consider this simply an instance of the RVic tendency to shake up established patterns; I doubt that the poet is attempting to draw a distinction between IndraтАЩs habitual roles as drinker, smiter, and goer, in contrast to a situational role as helper, as Tichy claims (Die Nomen agentis auf -tar- im Vedischen, 298-99; cf. 257 and passim). Among other things, тАЬhelpтАЭ is one of the most frequent things we ask Indra to do for us; it is surely one of his standard, habitual roles. It happens that there is no root-accented *├бvitar-, though avit├бr- is extremely common, and so no such form was available to match the first three -tar- stems in this vs. I do not know if the gap is accidental or systemic.

Note that k─Бr├║dh─Бyas-, a rare bv., reappears here from 12 – again, a possible reason for attaching this tс╣Ыca to the preceding one.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this ambrosia, the appropriate beverage of Indra, of which is fond, be quaffed (by him), so that it may inspire the divinity with favourable feelings (towards us), and that he may remove from us our adversaries, and (all) iniquity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here is this drinking cup, giving drink to Indra. IndraтАЩs dear immortal (drink) has been drunk,
so that it will exhilarate the god for the sake of his good favor and will keep hatred and constraint away from us. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes ├нndrasya as agent of ap─Бyi (тАЬIndra hat seinen lieben G├╢ttertrank getrunkenтАЭ), but finite passives, even verbs of consumption, donтАЩt take genitive agents.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the power of soma to rouse Indra to beneficial action is the general subject of the tс╣Ыca. The three forms belonging to тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ in the 1st hemistich, p─Б╠Бtram тАШdrinking cupтАЩ, indrap─Б╠Бnam тАШgiving drink to IndraтАЩ, and ap─Бyi тАШhas been drunkтАЩ, in echoing the first word of the preceding vs. (15a p─Б╠Бt─Б тАШdrinkerтАЩ), may have caused this tс╣Ыca to be grafted onto the last.

Griffith

The cup whence Indra drinks the draught is present: the Amrta dear to Indra hath been drunken,
That it may cheer the God to gracious favour, and keep far from us hatred and affliction.

Geldner

Dies ist die Schale, aus der Indra trinkt. Indra hat seinen lieben G├╢ttertrank getrunken, auf da├Я er den Gott zu guter Laune begeistere und er die Anfeindung, die Not von uns abwehre.

Grassmann

Es dient der Becher hier zum Trunk dem Indra, dem Indra lieb ward G├╢ttertrank getrunken; Damit den Gott zum Frohsinn er berausche, er treibe Noth von uns hinweg und Feindschaft.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExhilarated by it, valiant Maghavan, slay our unfriendly adversaries, whether kinsman or unrelated (to us); put to flight, Indra, hostile armies menacing us (with their weapons), and slay them.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Becoming exhilarated by it, o champion, smash your rivals and your foes, both kin and non-kin, o bounteous one.
Those with weapons aimed at us, setting their sights on usтАФpulverize and smash them, Indra, (for them to become) far away. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The object phrase in the 1st hemistich provides an ex. of number disharmony (of a different type from that in vs. 13). The main objects of IndraтАЩs smiting are тАЬrivals (and) foes,тАЭ the pl. phrase ┼Ы├бtr┼лn тАж am├нtr─Бn, but they are further specified as тАЬkin and non-kin,тАЭ j─Бm├нm ├бj─Бmim, in the singular. The same disharmony is found in IV.4.5 j─Бm├нm ├бj─Бmim тАж ┼Ы├бtr┼лn, where the ┼Ы├бtr┼лn that closes our p─Бda a substitutes for am├нtr─Бn.

17-18 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. contain two exx. of unexpectedly accented 2nd sg.

impvs.: 17a jah├н and 18d kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н, both internal to the p─Бda and preceded by material belonging to the same clause. Oldenberg cites both (in a list of other puzzling passages; ZDMG 60: 736), but provides no real explanation. In both cases it is possible to construct ad hoc justifications. For the jah├н of 17a, note that 17d also contains an accented form of this same impv. (though with metrically lengthened final) in the sequence pr├б mс╣Ыс╣З─Б jah─л╠Бca, where jah─л╠Бcontrasts with the immediately preceding impv. pr├б mс╣Ыс╣З─Б and has its accent honestly, as it were. It could be that jah├н in p─Бda a received the accent redactionally or as a poetic imitation of the jah─л╠Бlater in the vs. As for kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н in 18d, it might be taken as contrastive with the (rather distant) imperativally used injunctive kaс╕е at the end of b to the same root; however, they are not used in the same idiom. ItтАЩs also worth noting that kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н is followed by particles that ordinarily take 2nd position in a clause (sm─Б no), and so kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н by default appears to be in 1st position. And both 17a jah├н and 18d kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н are right after the caesura. But none of these explanations seems sufficient – e.g., post-caesura position does not induce accent on verbs – and I think we must consider these two exx. as peculiarities of the composer of this tс╣Ыca.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the power of soma to rouse Indra to beneficial action is the general subject of the tс╣Ыca. The three forms belonging to тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ in the 1st hemistich, p─Б╠Бtram тАШdrinking cupтАЩ, indrap─Б╠Бnam тАШgiving drink to IndraтАЩ, and ap─Бyi тАШhas been drunkтАЩ, in echoing the first word of the preceding vs. (15a p─Б╠Бt─Б тАШdrinkerтАЩ), may have caused this tс╣Ыca to be grafted onto the last.

Griffith

Therewith enraptured, Hero, slay our foemen, the unfriendly, Maghavan be they kin or strangers,
Those who still aim their hostile darts to smite us, turn them to flight, O Indra, crush and kill them.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAffluent Indra, facilitate to us (the acquisition of) vast riches in these our battles; (enable us) to gain the victory; make us prosperous with rain, and with sons and grandsons.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Once more, in these our battles, bounteous Indra, make for us a great wide space and easy passage.
Go halves with our patrons, Indra, in the conquering of the waters, of life and lineage. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the idiom in s┼лr─л╠Бn kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н тАж ardh├бm, cf. II.30.5 asm─Б╠Бn ardh├бm krс╣З╠е ut─Бt.

17-18 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. contain two exx. of unexpectedly accented 2nd sg.

impvs.: 17a jah├н and 18d kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н, both internal to the p─Бda and preceded by material belonging to the same clause. Oldenberg cites both (in a list of other puzzling passages; ZDMG 60: 736), but provides no real explanation. In both cases it is possible to construct ad hoc justifications. For the jah├н of 17a, note that 17d also contains an accented form of this same impv. (though with metrically lengthened final) in the sequence pr├б mс╣Ыс╣З─Б jah─л╠Бca, where jah─л╠Бcontrasts with the immediately preceding impv. pr├б mс╣Ыс╣З─Б and has its accent honestly, as it were. It could be that jah├н in p─Бda a received the accent redactionally or as a poetic imitation of the jah─л╠Бlater in the vs. As for kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н in 18d, it might be taken as contrastive with the (rather distant) imperativally used injunctive kaс╕е at the end of b to the same root; however, they are not used in the same idiom. ItтАЩs also worth noting that kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н is followed by particles that ordinarily take 2nd position in a clause (sm─Б no), and so kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н by default appears to be in 1st position. And both 17a jah├н and 18d kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н are right after the caesura. But none of these explanations seems sufficient – e.g., post-caesura position does not induce accent on verbs – and I think we must consider these two exx. as peculiarities of the composer of this tс╣Ыca.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet your vigorous steeds, harnessed of their own will, drawing your wish-bestowing chariot, guided by shower-yielding reins, quick-moving, hastening towards us, youthful, thunder-bearing, well-yoked, bring you to the hountiful, exhilarating (libation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your fallow bays, the bulls that have been yoked, the steeds with their bullish chariot and with their bullish reins,
the bulls that convey your maceтАФlet them, well-yoked, convey you here in our direction for bullish exhilaration. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca has a more obvious unifying feature than the last several: the repeated тАШbullтАЩ words, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- and vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б-. I count 16 exx. of the two stems in the three vss. The bull(ish) grammatical subjects of the three vss. are different: 19 IndraтАЩs horses, 20 the soma drinks, 21 Indra himself. The vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- stem predominates; vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- only appears beginning in the last p─Бda of 20 (though prepared for by instr.

pl. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гabhiс╕е in 20c). I do not see any appreciable difference in their usage; note the coreferential dative vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зe тАж vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б╠Бya in 20d and, even more striking, the use of the two stems in strictly parallel expressions in 21a and b: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б тАж div├│ vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бс╕е pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬthe bull of heaven, the bull of earthтАЭ and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б s├нndh┼лn─Бс╣Г vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б st├нy─Бn─Бm тАЬthe bull of the rivers and the bull of the standing waters.тАЭ Nonetheless, Geldner carefully distinguishes them, with Bull reserved for vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- rendered as Riese / riesig тАШgiantтАЩ. But I very much doubt if the intent was тАЬyou are the giant of heaven, the bull of the earth,тАЭ etc.

The concentration on the bull words leaves little room or energy for other poetic flourishes.

Griffith

Let thy Bay Stallions, harnessed, bring thee hither, Steeds with strong chariot and strong reins to hold them,
Strong Horses, speeding hither, bearing thunder, well-harnessed, for the strong exciting potion.

Geldner

Dich sollen die angeschirrten riesigen Falben, die Renner mit dem riesigen Wagen, mit den riesigen Z├╝geln, die riesigen, die deine Keule fahren, die Gutgeschirrten zu uns her fahren zu riesiger Trunkesfreude.

Grassmann

Her m├╢gen dich die starken F├╝chse fahren, mit starkem Strang geschirrt an starken Wagen, Zu uns gewandt die Hengste, Blitze tragend, zum starken Rauschtrank, sch├╢ngeschirrt die starken.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬShowerer (of benefits), your vigorous water-shedding steeds, like the waves (of the sea), exulting, are harnessed to your car; for they, (the priests), offer to you, the showerer (of benefits), ever youthful, the libation of the Soma expressed by the stones.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The bulls have mounted the wooden cup for you, o bull, like waves spraying ghee as they bring exhilaration.
Indra, to you, the bullish bull, they present soma from out of the (drops) pressed by bulls. с│У

Although they belong to different, and distant, tс╣Ыcas, the partitive gen. construction here, тАж pr├б тАж sut─Б╠Бn─Бm, DAT bharanti тАж, matches that in vs. 13: тАж pr├б тАж sut─Б╠Бn─Бm, DAT bhara тАж and occupies the same position in the vs., though in our vs. тИЪbhс╣Ы also has a direct acc. object s├│mam.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca has a more obvious unifying feature than the last several: the repeated тАШbullтАЩ words, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- and vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б-. I count 16 exx. of the two stems in the three vss. The bull(ish) grammatical subjects of the three vss. are different: 19 IndraтАЩs horses, 20 the soma drinks, 21 Indra himself. The vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- stem predominates; vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- only appears beginning in the last p─Бda of 20 (though prepared for by instr.

pl. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гabhiс╕е in 20c). I do not see any appreciable difference in their usage; note the coreferential dative vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зe тАж vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б╠Бya in 20d and, even more striking, the use of the two stems in strictly parallel expressions in 21a and b: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б тАж div├│ vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бс╕е pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬthe bull of heaven, the bull of earthтАЭ and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б s├нndh┼лn─Бс╣Г vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б st├нy─Бn─Бm тАЬthe bull of the rivers and the bull of the standing waters.тАЭ Nonetheless, Geldner carefully distinguishes them, with Bull reserved for vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- rendered as Riese / riesig тАШgiantтАЩ. But I very much doubt if the intent was тАЬyou are the giant of heaven, the bull of the earth,тАЭ etc.

The concentration on the bull words leaves little room or energy for other poetic flourishes.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, are the showerer of heaven, the bearer of earth, the feeder of the rivers, the supplier of the aggregated (waters); for you, showerer (of benefits), who are the most excellent shedder of rain, the sweet Soma, the honey-flavoured, is ready to be quaffed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Note the use of derivative of vс╣Ыс╣гa, to sprinkle, to rain; Indra’s horses are vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зa; they draw a vс╣Ыс╣гa ratha; and are guided by vс╣Ыс╣гarasmayaс╕е; again, the steeds are vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зa = nityat─Бruс╣Зnu, always young, and Indra is vс╣Ыс╣гan, vс╣Ыс╣г, and vс╣Ыс╣гabha, the showerer of rain or of benefits; perhaps, in all these metaphors, a grosser sense is perhaps implied

You are the bullish bull of heaven and of earth, the bullish bull of the rivers and of the standing waters.
O bull, for bullish you the drop has swelled, the sweet sap, the honeyed drink, to your liking. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Given the parallelism of the phrase vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б s├нndh┼лn─Бс╣Г vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б st├нy─Бn─Бm, it is clear that the gen. pl. st├нy─Бn─Бm must be in semantic complementarity with s├нndh┼лn─Бm тАШof the riversтАЩ. Almost the same pair is found in VII.5.2, with a substitution for the first nom.: net─Б╠Бs├нndh┼лn─Бс╣Г vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б st├нy─Бn─Бm. Grassmann glosses st├нy─Б- тАШSchneefeld, GletscherтАЩ, but, given the relative lack of attention to snow and the like in the RV once the Indo-Aryans had left the high mountains mostly behind, some other type of water contrasting with rivers seems more likely – with GeldnerтАЩs тАЬder stehenden Gew├дsserтАЭ a likely alternative (cf. also L├╝ders, Varuс╣Зa I.144). RenouтАЩs тАЬeauxstagnantesтАЭ (EVP XIII.56 and 141), though expressing a similar contrast, is less appealing because of the negative implication of тАЬstagnant watersтАЭ: would Indra really want to be their bull? The question then is what the form is derived from; EWA classifies it with the root тИЪsty─Б тАШbe stiffтАЩ, of limited attestation in Skt. but found also in MIA, which seems reasonable. However, I am tempted to see a primary or secondary association with тИЪsth─Б тАШstandтАЩ, since forms of this root (with the sense тАШstand stillтАЩ) can be used of waters. Cf., e.g., the famous phrase describiing the rushing of the waters freed by Indra in the Vс╣Ыtra battle in I.32.10 ├бtiс╣гс╣нс╕еant─лn─Бm тАЬof those (waters) not standing still.тАЭ Renou (EVP XIII.141) in a lapidary comment – тАЬfait comme d├нya-тАЭ – seems to hint at a direct derivation (d├нya- to тИЪd─Б, then st├нya- to тИЪsth─Б) without pursuing it, and Lubotsky (System, 104) tentatively suggests that it belongs to an *-i-enlarged form of тИЪ*steh2, viz. *steh2-i-, but doesnтАЩt further spell out the details. The trick of course is to keep the laryngeal from aspirating the t; if we start with LubotskyтАЩs root, the zero-grade *sth2-i- would presumably metathesize to *stih2 (as with тИЪp─Б(y) тАШdrinkтАЩ: p─лt├б-), which would yield stiy- before a vowel. But I have no commitment to such an analysis. In any case it is impossible to tell whether the form belongs to a short or a long a/─Б stem, since it only shows up in the gen. pl.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca has a more obvious unifying feature than the last several: the repeated тАШbullтАЩ words, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- and vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б-. I count 16 exx. of the two stems in the three vss. The bull(ish) grammatical subjects of the three vss. are different: 19 IndraтАЩs horses, 20 the soma drinks, 21 Indra himself. The vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- stem predominates; vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- only appears beginning in the last p─Бda of 20 (though prepared for by instr.

pl. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гabhiс╕е in 20c). I do not see any appreciable difference in their usage; note the coreferential dative vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зe тАж vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б╠Бya in 20d and, even more striking, the use of the two stems in strictly parallel expressions in 21a and b: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б тАж div├│ vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бс╕е pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬthe bull of heaven, the bull of earthтАЭ and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б s├нndh┼лn─Бс╣Г vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б st├нy─Бn─Бm тАЬthe bull of the rivers and the bull of the standing waters.тАЭ Nonetheless, Geldner carefully distinguishes them, with Bull reserved for vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- rendered as Riese / riesig тАШgiantтАЩ. But I very much doubt if the intent was тАЬyou are the giant of heaven, the bull of the earth,тАЭ etc.

The concentration on the bull words leaves little room or energy for other poetic flourishes.

English translation:

тАЬThis divine Soma, with Indra for its ally, crushed, as soon as genitive rated, Paс╣Зi by force; this Soma baffled the devices and the weapons of the malignant secreter of (the stolen) wealth, (the cattle).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This god here, being born with strength, with Indra as his yokemate, blocked the Paс╣Зi [/niggard]. This one here, the drop, stole the weapons of his own father, the tricks of the unkindly one. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, ├нnduс╕е тАШdropтАЩ opening p─Бda b firmly identifies the subject as Soma, but the common word play between phonologically similar ├нndu- and ├нndra-, found esp. in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX, underlines the permeable boundary just noted between Indra and Soma in this tс╣Ыca.

The brief narrative allusion in p─Бda c (тАЬstole the weapons of his own fatherтАЭ) sounds like a fractured version of the just-born Indra stealing the soma from Tvaс╣гс╣нar, but it is hard to know how to square that tale with this formulation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, repetition also characterizes this tс╣Ыca: the ay├бm that opens every hemistich, along with two other p─Бdas (23b, 24b). In all instances the referent is Soma, whose name, however, does not appear until the opening of the last p─Бda, 24d (though the reliable synonym ├нndu- тАШdropтАЩ is found in 22d). The beginning of the first vs., 22a, identifies the subject as a god (ay├бс╣Г dev├бс╕е), and the tс╣Ыca attributes powerful agency to him, including deeds generally associated with Indra, such as the defeat of the Paс╣Зi (22b), the placing of light in the sun (23b), and the propping apart of the two worlds (24a). It is only the specification of Indra (in an oblique case) as the тАЬyokemateтАЭ of тАЬthis godтАЭ early in the tс╣Ыca (22b ├нndreс╣Зa yuj─Б╠Б) that prevents the audience from assuming that ay├бс╣Г dev├бс╕е refers to Indra (who is, after all, the dedicand of the hymn). Nonetheless, the virtual identification of Soma with Indra is clear.

Griffith

This God, with might, when first he had his being, with Indra for ally, held fast the Pani.
This Indu stole away the warlike weapons, and foiled the arts of his malignant father.

Dieser Gott, unter Kraftanstrengung geboren, hat mit Indra als Verb├╝ndetem den Pani gel├дhmt. Dieser Saft stahl dem eigenen Vater die Waffen, die Zauberk├╝nste des Feindseligen.

Grassmann

Indu, der Gott, er, der durch Kraft geborne, er fesselte den Dieb im Bund mit Indra, Des eignen Vaters Waffen raubte Indu und tilgte aus des Unholds Zauberk├╝nste.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Soma made the dawns happily wedded to the sun; this Soma plural ced the light within the solar orb; this (Soma) has found the threefold ambrosia hidden in heaven in the three bright regions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ayam tridh─Бtu divi rocaneс╣гu, triteс╣гu, triteс╣гu vindat amс╣Ыtam nig┼лс╕╖ham = Soma becomes as it were ambrosia when received or concealed in the vessels at the three diurnal ceremonies, which ambrosia is properly deposited with the gods abiding in the third bright sphere, or in heaven

Jamison Brereton

This one gave the dawns a good husband; this one placed light within the sun.
This one found the threefold immortal one hidden in heaven among the third realms of light. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner points out (n. 23cd), in the 2nd hemistich Soma the god is differentiated from soma the drink, with the god finding the distant, hidden drink.

trit├йс╣гu is the only pl. form to this stem in the RV, and it is not at all clear what it is doing here. Geldner takes it as the PN Trita, with the pl. referring to Trita and his brothers, among whom Soma (the god) finds soma (the drink). But I know of no such narrative, and Geldner does not cite one. I take the form instead as representing the older adj. тАШthirdтАЩ (see EWA s.v.), the older correspondent of tс╣Ыt─л╠Бya- тАШthirdтАЩ (which, of course, is also old, having Iranian cognates). As is well known, there are three heavens, and I take the тАЬthird realms of lightтАЭ to be the third or highest heaven, here in the pl. because it is conceived of as further subdivided. For soma as resident in the third heaven, see K. Klaus, Die altindische Kosmologie, 175 with n. 66. It is possible (but only possible) that the vs. implicitly depicts the three heavens, with the dawns in the nearer one, the sun in the middle, and the soma in the third. The drink is threefold presumably because of the three pressings of the soma sacrifice.

22-24 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, repetition also characterizes this tс╣Ыca: the ay├бm that opens every hemistich, along with two other p─Бdas (23b, 24b). In all instances the referent is Soma, whose name, however, does not appear until the opening of the last p─Бda, 24d (though the reliable synonym ├нndu- тАШdropтАЩ is found in 22d). The beginning of the first vs., 22a, identifies the subject as a god (ay├бс╣Г dev├бс╕е), and the tс╣Ыca attributes powerful agency to him, including deeds generally associated with Indra, such as the defeat of the Paс╣Зi (22b), the placing of light in the sun (23b), and the propping apart of the two worlds (24a). It is only the specification of Indra (in an oblique case) as the тАЬyokemateтАЭ of тАЬthis godтАЭ early in the tс╣Ыca (22b ├нndreс╣Зa yuj─Б╠Б) that prevents the audience from assuming that ay├бс╣Г dev├бс╕е refers to Indra (who is, after all, the dedicand of the hymn). Nonetheless, the virtual identification of Soma with Indra is clear.

Griffith

The Dawns he wedded to a glorious Consort, and set within the Sun the light that lights him.
He found in heaven, in the third lucid regions, the threefold Amrta in its close concealment.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis (Soma) has been fixed heaven and earth; this has harnessed the seven-rayed chariot (of the sun); this Soma has developed of its own will the mature deeply-organized secretion in the kind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This has fixed heaven: these functions are ascribed to the Soma as being the source of the energies of Indra, who is the real agent, both in this and the preceding verse; this Indra has made the heavens etc.; deeply-organized secretion: da┼Ыayantram utsam = a well with ten machines;

Utsa = utsaraс╣Зa┼Ы─лlam, having the property of flowing forth, payas, milk; the epithet da┼Ыayantram is intriguing: it may imply aggregated bodily existence, or organs and functions of the body, which are the result of the nutriment furnished to the child by the matured milk agreeably to a khila, or cakс╣гu┼Ыca ┼Ыrotram ca mana┼Ыca pr─Бс╣З─Бpanau, deha, idam ┼Ыar─лram dvau prat ya├▒c─Бvanulomau visarg─Бv-etam tam manye di┼Ыayantram utsam, I consider the eye, the ear, the mind, the speech, the two vital airs, the form, the body, the two creations inverted and direct, as the tenfold utsa, or state of being; or, perhaps Soma is being offered with nine texts to Indra and other deities at the morning sacrifice (Aitareya Br─Бhman.a 3.1)

Jamison Brereton

This one propped apart heaven and earth; this one yoked the chariot with seven reins.
This one, Soma, by his ability, secures the cooked (milk) within the
cows, the wellspring with its ten fastenings: Soma! с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

(v├н) с╣гkabh─Бyat echoes astabh─Бyat in the first vs. of the tс╣Ыca (22b).

I will not speculate on the numerology in sapt├бra┼Ыmi- тАШhaving seven reinsтАЩ and da┼Ыayantra- тАШhaving ten fasteningsтАЩ, whose referents may be ritual or cosmological, or (most likely) both.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, repetition also characterizes this tс╣Ыca: the ay├бm that opens every hemistich, along with two other p─Бdas (23b, 24b). In all instances the referent is Soma, whose name, however, does not appear until the opening of the last p─Бda, 24d (though the reliable synonym ├нndu- тАШdropтАЩ is found in 22d). The beginning of the first vs., 22a, identifies the subject as a god (ay├бс╣Г dev├бс╕е), and the tс╣Ыca attributes powerful agency to him, including deeds generally associated with Indra, such as the defeat of the Paс╣Зi (22b), the placing of light in the sun (23b), and the propping apart of the two worlds (24a). It is only the specification of Indra (in an oblique case) as the тАЬyokemateтАЭ of тАЬthis godтАЭ early in the tс╣Ыca (22b ├нndreс╣Зa yuj─Б╠Б) that prevents the audience from assuming that ay├бс╣Г dev├бс╕е refers to Indra (who is, after all, the dedicand of the hymn). Nonetheless, the virtual identification of Soma with Indra is clear.

Griffith

He stayed and held the heaven and earth asunder: the chariot with the sevenfold reins he harnessed.
This Soma Set with power within the milch-kine a spring whose ripe contents ten fingers empty.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЕрдпрдореН) рдпрд╣ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдФрд░ рднреВрдорд┐ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖ рдХрд░рдХреЗ (рд╕реНрдХрднрд╛рдпрддреН) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рдЕрдпрдореН) рдпрд╣ рд╕рдм рдХреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рд╕рдкреНрддрд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдореН) рд╕рд╛рдд рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реВрдк рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрдВ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдореЗрдВ рдЙрд╕ (рд░рдердореН) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд▓реЛрдХ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдпреБрдирдХреН) рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рдЕрдпрдореН) рдпрд╣ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдФрд░ рдирд╣реАрдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рд╕реЛрдордГ) рд╕рдм рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╢рдЪреНрдпрд╛) рд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд░реНрдореНрдо рд╕реЗ (рдЧреЛрд╖реБ) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдзреЗрдиреБ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ (рдЙрддреНрд╕рдореН) рдХреВрдк рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдЬрд▓ рд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡реЗрджрд┐рдд рдХреЛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рджрд╢рдпрдиреНрддреНрд░рдореН) рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдо рдФрд░ рд╕реНрдереВрд▓ рджрд╢ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рднреВрдд рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреА рдпрдиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдд рдЬрд┐рд╕рдореЗрдВ рдЙрд╕ (рдкрдХреНрд╡рдореН) рдкрдХреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдХреЛ (рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рднреА рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ реереирекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреЛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдп рдХреЛ, рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдХреНрд╖рдорд╛ рдХреЛ, рд╕рдм рдХреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдФрд░ рджреБрдЧреНрдз рдЖрджрд┐ рд░рд╕реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдФрд░ рд╕рдм рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреЛ рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреН рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рдг рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рднреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕рдм рдХреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рд┐рдпреЗ реереирекрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░, рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЪрд╡рд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпрдерд╛рд╜рдпрдореАрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЛ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдХрднрд╛рдпрджрдпрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдВ рд░рдердордпреБрдирдЧрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдордГ рд╢рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЧреЛрд╖реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд░реБрддреНрд╕рдорд┐рд╡ рджрд╢рдпрдиреНрддреНрд░рдВ рдкрдХреНрд╡рдВ рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░ рддрдерд╛ рдпреВрдпрдордкрд┐ рдзрд░рдд реереирекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреЗрд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдпрдореН) (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рднреВрдореА (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг (рд╕реНрдХрднрд╛рдпрддреН) рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ (рдЕрдпрдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдзрд░реНрддреНрддреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ (рд░рдердореН) рд░рдордгреАрдпрд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХрдореН (рдЕрдпреБрдирдХреН) рдпреБрдирдХреНрддрд┐ (рд╕рдкреНрддрд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдореН) рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░рд╢реНрдордпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрдореН (рдЕрдпрдореН) рдзрд░рд╛рдзрд░рдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдЧреЛрд╖реБ) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрд╖реБ рдзреЗрдиреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ (рд╢рдЪреНрдпрд╛) рд╕рддреНрдпреЗрди рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ (рдкрдХреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рд╕реЛрдордГ) рдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдЧрддреН рд╕реВрддреЗ рд╕рдГ (рджрд╛рдзрд╛рд░) рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рддреБрдЬрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рджреИрд░реНрдШреНрдпрдореНред (рджрд╢рдпрдиреНрддреНрд░рдореН) рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╕реНрдереВрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рджрд╢рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрдиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрддреН (рдЙрддреНрд╕рдореН) рдХреВрдкрдорд┐рд╡ рдЬрд▓реЗрди рдХреНрд▓рд┐рдиреНрдирдореН реереирекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рдиреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрд╡рддреН рдХреНрд╖рдорд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рджреБрдЧреНрдзрд╛рджреАрдиреН рд░рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддреНрд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдЧрджреНрдпрдерд╛рд╡рдиреНрдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рдп рдзрд░рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдпреВрдпрдордкреНрдпреЗрддрддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдзрд░рддреЗрддрд┐ реереирекрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЧреБрдгрдХрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреЛ ! рдЬреЛ (рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдп (рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢) рд╡ рдкреГрдереНрд╡реАрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдХреНрд╖рдорд╛, рджреВрдз рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рд░рд╕ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЛ рд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдЬрдЧрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдпрдерд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рдг рдХрд░реВрди рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЛ рддрд╕реЗ рддреБрдореНрд╣реАрд╣реА рдпрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рд╛. рее реирек рее
